## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics / nonlinear oscillations
**Analysis**: The task models the acceleration dv_dt of a non-linear harmonic oscillator, governed by Newton's second law. The acceleration depends on restoring force (function of position x), damping (function of velocity v), and possibly external or parametric forcing (function of time t). Common physical structures involve linear and nonlinear stiffness, viscous and nonlinear drag, and periodic drives.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear undamped restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (linear stiffness with viscous damping)
- Duffing hardening spring: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinearity, no damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening spring with linear damping)
- Mathematical pendulum: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (nonlinear sine restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (selfŌĆæsustained limitŌĆæcycle oscillations)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (nonlinear damping proportional to v┬│)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (periodic external drive)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (nonlinear drag typical in fluidŌĆæresistant motion)
- Mathieu parametric oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (stiffness modulated by time)
- PositionŌĆædependent damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v - c3 * x**2 * v (dissipation varying with displacement)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Undamped conservative dynamics ŌåÆ acceleration depends only on position x, no v terms appear
- Linear restoring force ŌåÆ acceleration proportional to x with a negative coefficient
- Nonlinear stiffening/softening spring ŌåÆ odd power terms in x (e.g., x┬│, xŌüĄ) or saturating functions like tanh(c*x)
- PendulumŌĆælike largeŌĆæamplitude oscillations ŌåÆ sine of position, sin(c*x), as the restoring force
- Linear viscous damping ŌåÆ term proportional to -v with a positive rate coefficient
- Nonlinear damping (drag) ŌåÆ term proportional to -v*|v| or -v┬│ capturing velocityŌĆædependent dissipation
- SelfŌĆæsustained (limitŌĆæcycle) oscillations ŌåÆ velocity multiplied by a function of position, typically (1 - c*x┬▓)*v
- External periodic forcing ŌåÆ additive term of the form cos(c*t) or sin(c*t)
- Parametric excitation ŌåÆ position multiplied by a timeŌĆævarying coefficient, often periodic like (1 + c*cos(Žē*t))*x
- PositionŌĆædependent damping ŌåÆ mixed terms such as x┬▓*v, where dissipation grows with displacement
